###begin article-title 0
###xml 37 57 37 57 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 140 144 140 144 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 149 153 149 153 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp6</italic>
###xml 37 57 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
The complete mitochondrial genome of Evania appendigaster (Hymenoptera: Evaniidae) has low A+T content and a long intergenic spacer between atp8 and atp6
###end article-title 0
###begin p 1
###xml 214 234 214 234 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 579 583 579 583 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad1</italic>
###xml 644 649 644 649 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>
###xml 654 658 654 658 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnK</italic>
###xml 737 742 737 742 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>
###xml 939 943 939 943 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 948 952 948 952 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp6</italic>
###xml 1063 1068 1063 1068 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS1</italic>
###xml 1073 1077 1073 1077 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad1</italic>
###xml 214 234 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
The apocritan Hymenoptera show extraordinary features in mitochondrial genomes, but no complete sequence has been reported for the basal lineage, Evanioidea. Here, we sequenced the complete mitochondrial genome of Evania appendigaster. This genome is 17,817 bp long; with low A+T content, 77.8%, compared with other hymenopteran species. Four tRNA genes were rearranged, among which remote inversion is the dominant gene rearrangement event. Gene shuffling is caused by tandem duplication-random loss while remote inversion is best explained by recombination. The start codon of nad1 was found as TTG, which might be common across Hymenoptera. trnS2 and trnK use abnormal anticodons TCT and TTT, respectively, and the D-stem pairings in trnS2 are absent. The secondary structure of two rRNA genes are predicted and compared with those in other insects. Five long intergenic spacers were present, including a long intergenic spacer between atp8 and atp6, where these two genes overlap in the previously reported animal genomes. A conserved motif was found between trnS1 and nad1, which is proposed to be associated with mtTERM. The A+T-rich region is 2,325 bp long, among the longest in insects, and contains a tandem repeat region.
###end p 1
###begin title 2
Keywords
###end title 2
###begin title 3
Introduction
###end title 3
###begin p 4
###xml 165 166 165 166 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR1">1</xref>
###xml 168 169 168 169 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
###xml 285 286 285 286 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR3">3</xref>
###xml 288 289 288 289 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR4">4</xref>
###xml 403 404 403 404 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR5">5</xref>
Animal mitochondrial genomes are about 16 Kb in size and contain 37 genes: 13 protein-coding genes, 22 transfer RNA genes (tRNA) and two ribosomal RNA genes (rRNA) [1, 2]. The genome is highly economized with few sections of noncoding DNA, intergenic regions, or repetitive sequences [3, 4], except for an A+T rich region, which contains essential regulatory elements for transcription and replication [5].
###end p 4
###begin p 5
###xml 63 64 63 64 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>
###xml 115 116 115 116 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR6">6</xref>
###xml 117 119 117 119 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR12">12</xref>
###xml 226 228 226 228 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR13">13</xref>
###xml 229 231 229 231 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR16">16</xref>
###xml 350 352 350 352 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR10">10</xref>
###xml 354 356 354 356 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">17</xref>
###xml 386 388 386 388 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR18">18</xref>
###xml 389 391 389 391 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR22">22</xref>
###xml 832 834 832 834 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 836 838 836 838 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR24">24</xref>
###xml 940 942 940 942 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">17</xref>
Gene arrangements are usually conserved within major lineages [2], but may be highly rearranged in certain groups [6-12]. Gene rearrangement events may serve as useful phylogenetic markers and models for evolutionary studies [13-16]. In apocritan Hymenoptera, frequent gene rearrangements have been observed from broad examinations of gene segments [10, 17] and whole genome sequences [18-22]. However, no informative arrangement pattern has been identified to date, for which there are two possible explanations: the one is that diversified gene arrangements have arisen independently among different hymenopteran lineages, and the other is that limited sampling is concealing potentially synapomorphic rearrangements. The apocritan lineage shows other extraordinary features in the mitochondrial genome, such as high A+T content [23, 24], diversified gene rearrangement events, and the involvement of recombination in gene rearrangement [17].
###end p 5
###begin p 6
###xml 75 77 75 77 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR25">25</xref>
###xml 79 81 79 81 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR26">26</xref>
###xml 294 314 294 314 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 294 314 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
Evaniidae is proposed to be one of the most basal lineages in Hymenoptera [25, 26]. Presently, no complete mitochondrial genome has been sequenced from members of this family or its presumed sister groups, the Aulacidae and Gasteruptiidae. Here, we present the complete mitochondrial genome of Evania appendigaster (Hymenoptera: Evaniidae) and give a thorough description of its genome features in comparison to other hymenopteran species.
###end p 6
###begin title 7
Materials and methods
###end title 7
###begin title 8
DNA extraction, PCR amplification and sequencing
###end title 8
###begin p 9
###xml 103 119 103 119 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 103 119 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
Total genomic DNA was extracted using the DNeasy tissue kit (Qiagen, Hilden, Germany) from a leg of an E. appendigaster adult.
###end p 9

###xml 478 982 478 982 <table-wrap xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="Tab1"><label>Table&#160;1</label><caption><p textid="11">Primers used in this study</p></caption><table frame="hsides" rules="groups"><thead><tr><th align="left">Region</th><th align="left">Primer position</th><th align="left">Product length (bp)</th><th align="left" rowspan="2"><italic>rrnL-rrnS</italic></td><td char="&#8211;" align="char" rowspan="2">13034&#8211;15118</td><td char="." align="char" rowspan="2">2085</td><td rowspan="2">14700&#8211;15275</td><td char="." align="char" rowspan="2">576</td><td align="left">GTATAYTTACTTTGTTACGACTT</td></tr><tr><td align="left">GTGCCAGCAGYYGCGGTTANAC</td></tr><tr><td align="left" rowspan="2"><italic>rrnS-cox1</italic></td><td char="&#8211;" align="char" rowspan="2">15096&#8211;2334</td><td char="." align="char" rowspan="2">5057</td><td align="left">ATTAGGGTATCTAATCCAACTTT</td></tr><tr><td align="left">GCTCGTGTATCCACATCTATT</td></tr></tbody></table></table-wrap>
A range of universal insect mitochondrial primers [27, 28] and hymenopteran mitochondrial primers were used to amplify the regions of cox1-cox2, cob-rrnL, rrnL-rrnS. Species-specific primers were designed based on sequenced fragments and combined in various ways to bridge the gap of cox2-cob and rrnS-cox1. Six fragments of 575-8626 bp were amplified, covering the whole mitochondrial genome (Table 1). The PCR and sequencing procedures followed the methods in Wei et al. [23].Table 1Primers used in this studyRegionPrimer positionProduct length (bp)Primer sequencecox1-cox22127-36341508TATTTTGATTYTTTGGHCAYCCWGAAGTCCACAAATTTCTGAACATTGcox2-cob3339-119648626TCAGGTCACCAATGATATTGAATTACACCTCCTAGTTTATTAGGGATcob-rrnL11480-135932114TATGTACTACCATGAGGACAAATATCTTACCTTAGGGATAACAGCGTWArrnL-rrnS13034-151182085CCWGGTAAAATTAAAATATAAACTTCAAACTAGGATTAGATACCCTATTATrrnS14700-15275576GTATAYTTACTTTGTTACGACTTGTGCCAGCAGYYGCGGTTANACrrnS-cox115096-23345057ATTAGGGTATCTAATCCAACTTTGCTCGTGTATCCACATCTATT
###end p 10

Primers used in this study
###end p 11
###begin title 12
Genome annotation and secondary structure prediction
###end title 12
###begin p 13
###xml 74 76 74 76 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR29">29</xref>
###xml 354 356 354 356 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR30">30</xref>
###xml 442 444 442 444 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 666 671 666 671 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>
###xml 776 778 776 778 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR31">31</xref>
tRNA genes were initially identified using the tRNAscan-SE search server [29] with default parameters. Sequences longer than 100 bp between the identified tRNA genes were used as queries in BLAST searches in GenBank for identification of protein-coding and rRNA genes. The exact initiation and termination codons were identified in ClustalX version 2.0 [30] using reference sequences from other insects, following the criteria in Wei et al. [23]. Finally, the tRNA search was carried out again for the large intergenic regions using a reduced cutoff score. Twenty-one of the 22 typical animal mitochondrial tRNA genes were found using the previous steps, except for trnS2, which was identified by alignment. A+T content and codon usage were calculated using MEGA version 4.0 [31].
###end p 13
###begin p 14
###xml 82 84 82 84 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR29">29</xref>
###xml 97 102 97 102 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>
###xml 225 227 225 227 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
All tRNA secondary structures were predicted using the tRNAscan-SE search server [29] except for trnS2, which was predicted manually. rRNA structures were predicted by comparison and algorithm-based methods as in Wei et al. [23].
###end p 14

Results and discussion
###end title 15

###xml 37 53 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 281 301 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
###xml 933 953 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
The complete mitochondrial genome of E. appendigaster is 17,817 bp (GenBank accession No. FJ593187), which is among the largest animal mitochondrial genomes yet sequenced [1]. All of the 37 typical animal mitochondrial genes were identified (Fig. 1; Table 2).Fig. 1Organization of Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome. Gene abbreviations are as follows: cox1, cox2, and cox3 refer to the cytochrome oxidase subunits, cob refers to cytochrome b, nad1-nad6 refer to NADH dehydrogenase components, and rrnL and rrnS refer to ribosomal RNAs. Transfer RNA genes are denoted by one letter symbol according to the IPUC-IUB single-letter amino acid codes. L1, L2, S1 and S2 denote tRNALeu(CUN), tRNALeu(UUR), tRNASer(AGY) and tRNASer(UCN), respectively. AT indicates A+T-rich region. Gene names with lines indicate that the genes are coded on the minority strand while those without lines are on the majority strandTable 2Annotation of Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genomeGeneStrandGene positionGene length (bp)Anti/Start codonStop codonIntergenic nucleotidestrnC+1-6363GCA--2trnM+64-12966CAT-0trnI+128-19467GAT--1trnS1-194-26269TGA--2trnQ-261-33070TTG-22nad2+353-13651013ATGTA-2trnY-1364-143269GTA-3cox1+1436-29801545ATGTAA-5trnL2+2976-304166TAA-0cox2+3042-3719678ATTTAA8trnK+3728-379770TTT-534trnD+4332-439362GTC-0atp8+4394-4555162ATGTAA244atp6+4800-5474675ATTTAA1cox3+5476-6265790ATAT0trnG+6266-633267TCC-0nad3+6333-6683351ATTTAA11trnA+6695-676268TGC-20trnR+6783-684866TCG--6trnN+6843-690866GTT--3trnS2+6906-696661TCT-0trnE+6967-703266TTC-2trnF-7035-709965GAA-0nad5-7100-87471648ATATAA-3trnH-8745-881268GTG-0nad4-8813-101481336ATGT-7nad4l-10142-10414273ATTTAA1trnT+10416-1048065TGT-0trnP-10481-1054666TGG-2nad6+10549-11088540ATCTAA1cob+11090-122531164ATGTAA94nad1-12348-13273926TTGTA0trnL1-13274-1334269TAG-0rrnL-13343-146161274--0trnV-14617-1468064TAC-0rrnS-14681-15427747--0trnW-15428-1549265TCA-0A+T-rich region-15493-178172325--0+ Indicates the gene coded on the majority strand- Indicates the gene coded on the minority strand- Indicates the strand or codon not applicable; the abbreviations are as in Fig. 1

###xml 607 620 607 620 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">without lines</italic>
###xml 16 36 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
Organization of Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome. Gene abbreviations are as follows: cox1, cox2, and cox3 refer to the cytochrome oxidase subunits, cob refers to cytochrome b, nad1-nad6 refer to NADH dehydrogenase components, and rrnL and rrnS refer to ribosomal RNAs. Transfer RNA genes are denoted by one letter symbol according to the IPUC-IUB single-letter amino acid codes. L1, L2, S1 and S2 denote tRNALeu(CUN), tRNALeu(UUR), tRNASer(AGY) and tRNASer(UCN), respectively. AT indicates A+T-rich region. Gene names with lines indicate that the genes are coded on the minority strand while those without lines are on the majority strand
###end p 18

###xml 14 34 14 34 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 14 34 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
Annotation of Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome
###end p 19
###begin p 20
+ Indicates the gene coded on the majority strand
###end p 20
###begin p 21
- Indicates the gene coded on the minority strand
###end p 21
###begin p 22
###xml 81 82 81 82 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
- Indicates the strand or codon not applicable; the abbreviations are as in Fig. 1
###end p 22
###begin p 23
###xml 298 299 298 299 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab2" ref-type="table">2</xref>
There are in total 31 overlapping nucleotides between neighboring genes in nine locations and the length of overlapping sequence is 1-7 bp, while there are in total 943 bp intergenic nucleotides in 13 locations and the length of intergenic spacers is 1-534 bp, excluding the A+T-rich region (Table 2).
###end p 23

###xml 19 35 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
The A+T content of E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome are lower than all other sequenced hymenopteran species, and there are more A and C than T and G in the majority strand (Table 3). ###begin title 28
Gene rearrangement
###end title 28
###begin p 29
###xml 24 40 24 40 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 303 305 303 305 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">17</xref>
###xml 371 375 371 375 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnW</italic>
###xml 377 381 377 381 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnC</italic>
###xml 386 391 386 391 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS1</italic>
###xml 414 418 414 418 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnM</italic>
###xml 425 426 425 426 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig1" ref-type="fig">1</xref>
###xml 588 592 588 592 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>
###xml 594 598 594 598 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>
###xml 599 603 599 603 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">cox1</italic>
###xml 605 609 605 609 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">cox2</italic>
###xml 610 614 610 614 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 619 623 619 623 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad3</italic>
###xml 624 628 624 628 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad5</italic>
###xml 630 632 630 632 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR10">10</xref>
###xml 634 636 634 636 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">17</xref>
###xml 638 640 638 640 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 678 694 678 694 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 800 802 800 802 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR34">34</xref>
###xml 921 925 921 925 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">cox2</italic>
###xml 926 930 926 930 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 941 943 941 943 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR10">10</xref>
###xml 953 969 953 969 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 24 40 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 678 694 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 953 969 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
Gene arrangement of the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome is similar to other apocritan species. Gene rearrangement events have been classified as translocation, local inversion (inverted in the local position), gene shuffling (local translocation) and remote inversion (translocated and inverted) [17]. Four tRNA genes are rearranged, which are remote inversions of trnW, trnC and trnS1 and gene shuffling of trnM (Fig. 1). Rearrangement of tRNA genes is common in the hymenopteran mitochondrial genome, especially those in tRNA clusters, such as in the junctions of A+T-rich region-nad2, nad2-cox1, cox2-atp8 and nad3-nad5 [10, 17, 23]. However, the rearrangements in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome are novel. In vertebrates, gene shuffling is the dominant gene rearrangement event [34], while in Hymenoptera, equal numbers of gene shuffling, inversion and translocation events have been observed at the cox2-atp8 junction [10]. In the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome, remote inversion was found to be the dominant gene rearrangement event.
###end p 29
###begin p 30
###xml 88 90 88 90 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR17">17</xref>
###xml 92 94 92 94 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR35">35</xref>
###xml 389 393 389 393 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>
###xml 464 468 464 468 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnQ</italic>
###xml 473 477 473 477 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>
###xml 527 528 527 528 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Tab2" ref-type="table">2</xref>
###xml 708 712 708 712 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnC</italic>
###xml 717 722 717 722 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS1</italic>
###xml 774 778 774 778 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnM</italic>
###xml 823 827 823 827 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnI</italic>
###xml 828 832 828 832 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnQ</italic>
###xml 833 837 833 837 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnM</italic>
###xml 870 874 870 874 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnI</italic>
###xml 875 879 875 879 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnQ</italic>
###xml 884 888 884 888 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnM</italic>
###xml 960 964 960 964 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnC</italic>
###xml 969 974 969 974 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS1</italic>
###xml 1086 1088 1086 1088 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR36">36</xref>
###xml 1217 1221 1217 1221 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnQ</italic>
###xml 1226 1230 1226 1230 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>
###xml 1292 1296 1292 1296 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnM</italic>
Gene shuffling is usually explained by the tandem duplication-random loss (TDRL) model [17, 35]. Evidence of the TDRL model includes a derived pattern of gene order, pseudogene and the position of intergenic spacer, the last two of which are the expected intermediate steps in changing mitochondrial gene order under this model. In the derived tRNA cluster between the A+T-rich region and nad2, all neighboring genes are overlapped or directly adjacent except for trnQ and nad2, where there is a 22 bp intergenic spacer (Table 2). Under the TDRL model, it is unlikely to randomly delete the duplicated or original genes to produce a pattern in which remnant adjacent genes overlap. Thus, it is unlikely that trnC and trnS1 were rearranged by TDRL, while it is possible that trnM was rearranged by tandem duplication of the trnI-trnQ-trnM cluster followed by deletion of trnI-trnQ and trnM in the two boundaries in an intermediate state before the insertion of trnC and trnS1. This region is located to one side of the A+T rich region that is thought to contain two replication origins [36], so an illicit-primer may be responsible for the duplication of the original tRNA cluster. The 22 bp intergenic spacer between trnQ and nad2 may be a remnant region after deletion of the second copy of trnM. Recombination may be involved in remote inversions and is the most plausible explanation for local inversions in apocritan mitochondrial genomes.
###end p 30
###begin title 31
Protein-coding genes
###end title 31
###begin p 32
###xml 44 60 44 60 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 236 240 236 240 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad6</italic>
###xml 244 248 244 248 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 253 269 253 269 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 290 294 290 294 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 396 400 396 400 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 44 60 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 253 269 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
The size of the protein-coding genes in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome is similar to their corresponding orthologs in other insects. The genes with the highest A+T content in the hymenopteran mitochondrial genome are usually nad6 or atp8. In E. appendigaster, the A+T content of atp8 is 69.1%, amongst the lowest ones, and this is the result of lower A+T content in the 3' sequence of atp8.
###end p 32

###xml 1904 2240 1904 2240 <fig xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="Fig2"><label>Fig.&#160;2</label><caption><p textid="34">Determination of <italic>nad1</italic> start codons in <italic>Evania appendigaster</italic> and other reported hymenopteran mitochondrial genomes. ###xml 287 303 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 652 674 <span type="species:ncbi:32432">Vanhornia eucnemidarum</span>
###xml 684 700 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 1144 1156 <span type="species:ncbi:32411">Perga condei</span>
###xml 1163 1185 <span type="species:ncbi:32432">Vanhornia eucnemidarum</span>
###xml 1273 1293 <span type="species:ncbi:208481">Diadegma semiclausum</span>
###xml 1300 1316 <span type="species:ncbi:161221">Polistes humilis</span>
###xml 1332 1335 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">bee</span>
###xml 1432 1448 <span type="species:ncbi:485912">Abispa ephippium</span>
###xml 1453 1469 <span type="species:ncbi:161221">Polistes humilis</span>
###xml 1526 1538 <span type="species:ncbi:485912">A. ephippium</span>
###xml 1948 1968 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
All protein-coding genes start with ATN codons (two with ATA, four with ATT, one with ATC, and five with ATG) except for nad1, which uses TTG as start codon (Table 1). cox1 is usually found to use nonstandard start codons in insects, such as TCG, ACC, CGA, CTA, CCG and AAA [37, 38]. In E. appendigaster, cox1 uses the usual start codon ATG, 3 bp after the end of trnY, and the translated amino acid sequence aligned well with orthologs in other Hymenoptera. All examined species in Lepidoptera have been found to use R as the initial amino acid for cox1 [39], whereas in Hymenoptera all species uses the ATN start codon [18, 19, 21-23, 32] except for Vanhornia eucnemidarum [20]. In E. appendigaster, three ATA lying in or 6 bp downstream from trnL1 are possible start codons for nad1. However, we proposed TTG directly after trnL1 as the start codon for nad1. This would minimize intergenic spacer and avoid overlapping between trnL1 and nad1 [37, 40]. We examined nad1 start codons in the 11 previously reported hymenopteran species, and the results revealed that either the intergenic spacers or the overlapping regions would be reduced in Perga condei [32], Vanhornia eucnemidarum [20] and three Nasonia species [21] if TTG is assigned as the start codon (Fig. 2). In Diadegma semiclausum [23], Polistes humilis [22] and three bee species [18, 33], no TTG codon is found near the initial region of nad1. In two vespid species, Abispa ephippium and Polistes humilis, trnL1 is rearranged and rrnL is left upstream nad1. In A. ephippium, a TTG codon is present 3 bp downstream the identified start codon ATA. Since there is no standard way to define the exact boundaries of rRNAs, the criteria of reducing intergenic spacer and overlapping region could not be applied to assign the start codon. In conclusion, our results suggest that TTG is a possible start codon for nad1 in Hymenoptera [37, 40, 41].Fig. 2Determination of nad1 start codons in Evania appendigaster and other reported hymenopteran mitochondrial genomes. The box indicates the newly assigned start codons, and the shaded regions the previously assigned start codons. Sequences of tRNA are marked by solid lines, intergenic spacers by dotted lines and rrnL by dashed lines
###end p 33

###xml 337 353 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 386 406 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
Nine protein-coding genes use the termination codon TAA. Four protein-coding genes use incomplete stop codons: nad1 and nad2 use the truncated termination codon TA, and cox3 and nad4 use T, which is commonly reported in other invertebrates [18, 42]. ###begin title 38
tRNA genes
###end title 38
###begin p 39
###xml 107 112 107 112 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>

###xml 599 604 599 604 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>
###xml 648 650 648 650 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR37">37</xref>
###xml 754 760 754 760 <label xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fig.&#160;3</label>
###xml 824 844 824 844 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 927 932 927 932 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">lines</italic>

###xml 997 997 997 997 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="11033_2009_9640_Fig3_HTML" id="MO3"/>
###xml 754 997 754 997 <fig xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="Fig3"><label>Fig.&#160;3</label><caption><p textid="40">Predicted secondary structures for the 22 typical tRNA genes of <italic>Evania appendigaster</italic> mitochondrial genome. Base-pairing is indicated as follows: Watson&#8211;Crick pairs by <italic>lines</italic>, wobble GU pairs by <italic>dots</italic> and other noncanonical pairs by <italic>circles</italic></p></caption><graphic xlink:href="11033_2009_9640_Fig3_HTML" id="MO3"/></fig>
###xml 824 844 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
The length of tRNAs ranges from 61 to 70 bp. All tRNA genes have a typical cloverleaf structure except for trnS2 (Fig. 3). trnS2 could not be identified and folded using conventional tRNA search methods such as tRNAscan-SE. We manually found the location of trnS2 by comparisons with those identified in other insects and then determined the exact boundaries according to the secondary structure folded by eye. The D-stem pairings in the DHU arm are absent in E. appendigastertrnS2, which has also been reported in other insects [6, 18, 37, 43] and the rest of Metazoa [44, 45]. Since this atypical trnS2 is common in Coleoptera, Sheffield et al. [37] built an updated covariance model for automated annotation, which also performs well in other insects.Fig. 3Predicted secondary structures for the 22 typical tRNA genes of Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome. Base-pairing is indicated as follows: Watson-Crick pairs by lines, wobble GU pairs by dots and other noncanonical pairs by circles
###end p 39

###end p 40
###begin p 41
###xml 48 64 48 64 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 207 223 207 223 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 298 300 298 300 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">46</xref>
###xml 423 425 423 425 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR47">47</xref>
###xml 426 428 426 428 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR50">50</xref>
###xml 485 497 485 497 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Acanthamoeba</italic>
###xml 499 501 499 501 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR51">51</xref>
###xml 519 521 519 521 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR52">52</xref>
###xml 559 563 559 563 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnQ</italic>
###xml 565 569 565 569 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnR</italic>
###xml 574 579 574 579 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS1</italic>
###xml 741 757 741 757 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 780 782 780 782 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR53">53</xref>
###xml 48 64 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 207 223 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 741 757 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
A total of 28 unmatched base pairs exist in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial tRNA secondary structures, 19 of which are G-U pairs, eight U-U and one A-A. The number of mismatches is relatively high in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial tRNAs compared with other insects, and even within Metazoa [46]. Mismatches in regions where the tRNA genes overlap with adjacent downstream genes could be corrected by 3'-RNA editing [47-50]. The 5'-parts of tRNA accepter stems are also found in Acanthamoeba [51] and some fungi [52]. Of the 28 mismatches, only four in trnQ, trnR and trnS1 are located in the overlapping regions in the accepter stem, indicating that other mechanisms might be involved to escape the effects of Muller's ratchet in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome [53].
###end p 41
###begin p 42
###xml 0 5 0 5 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS2</italic>
###xml 10 14 10 14 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnK</italic>
###xml 130 132 130 132 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
trnS2 and trnK use abnormal anticodons TCT and TTT, respectively, which have been found to be correlated with gene rearrangement [23].
###end p 42
###begin title 43
rRNA genes
###end title 43
###begin p 44
###xml 0 4 0 4 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rrnL</italic>
###xml 60 64 60 64 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rrnS</italic>
rrnL has a length of 1274 bp, with an A+T content of 79.7%. rrnS has a length of 747 bp, with an A+T content of 76.0%. The gene sizes are normal, but the A+T contents are lower than their counterparts in other hymenopteran species.
###end p 44

###xml 658 664 658 664 <label xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fig.&#160;4</label>
###xml 674 678 674 678 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rrnL</italic>
###xml 702 722 702 722 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 807 823 807 823 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">continuous lines</italic>
###xml 825 826 825 826 <bold xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">A</bold>
###xml 838 842 838 842 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rrnL</italic>
###xml 844 845 844 845 <bold xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">B</bold>

###xml 904 905 904 905 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" rid="Fig2" ref-type="fig">2</xref>

###xml 183 198 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 208 220 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">A. mellifera</span>
###xml 400 416 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 428 443 <span type="species:ncbi:7227">D. melanogaster</span>
###xml 526 542 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 579 591 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">A. mellifera</span>
###xml 702 722 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
Both rrnL and rrnS conform to the secondary structure models proposed for these genes from other insects [23, 39, 54-56]. Forty-nine helices are present in E. appendigasterrrnL as in D. melanogaster [55] and A. mellifera [54], belonging to six domains (Fig. 4). H837 usually forms a long stem structure with a small loop in the terminal [23, 37, 54], but it forms a shorter stem and a larger loop in E. appendigaster as that in D. melanogaster [55]. The deduced structures of H2347 and H2520 are variable [54, 57, 58], but in E. appendigaster they are more similar to those from A. mellifera by Gillespie et al. (2006) than those from other insects [57, 58].Fig. 4Predicted rrnL secondary structure in Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome. Tertiary interactions and base triples are shown connected by continuous lines. A 5' half of rrnL; B 3' half of rrnL. Symbols for base-pairings are as in Fig. 2
###end p 45

###xml 63 73 <span type="species:ncbi:7244">D. virilis</span>
###xml 83 95 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">A. mellifera</span>
###xml 380 396 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 431 441 <span type="species:ncbi:7244">D. virilis</span>
###xml 493 507 <span type="species:ncbi:208481">D. semiclausum</span>
###xml 512 524 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">A. mellifera</span>
###xml 663 679 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 724 734 <span type="species:ncbi:7244">D. virilis</span>
###xml 744 758 <span type="species:ncbi:208481">D. semiclausum</span>
###xml 792 804 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">A. mellifera</span>
###xml 901 910 <span type="species:ncbi:7460">honey bee</span>
###xml 956 972 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 1084 1104 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
The secondary structure of rrnS contains 29 helices present in D. virilis [56] and A. mellifera [54], belonging to three domains (Fig. 5). Helix H39 could not be predicted, where a circle was formed by H27, H47, H367 and H500, and the sequences in between. Helix 47 is variable among different lepidopteran species, but the terminal portion of this stem is conserved [37], and in E. appendigaster, two loops were formed similar to D. virilis but different from two other hymenopteran species, D. semiclausum and A. mellifera, where a larger loop is present. H673 is well conserved in moths, where one stem with a bulge in the terminal is present [39, 59], and in E. appendigaster, two stem-loop structures are present as in D. virilis [56] and D. semiclausum [23], but different from that in A. mellifera [54], in which this structure is similar to moths. The structure of H1074 has been discussed in honey bee [54, 60, 61], and our predicted structure in E. appendigaster is consistent with that of Page (2000) and Gillespie et al. (2006).Fig. 5Predicted rrnS secondary structure in Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome. Symbols are as in Fig. 3
###end p 47

###begin title 49
Non-coding regions
###end title 49
###begin p 50
###xml 44 60 44 60 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">E. appendigaster</italic>
###xml 177 181 177 181 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnQ</italic>
###xml 186 190 186 190 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>
###xml 219 223 219 223 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnK</italic>
###xml 228 232 228 232 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnD</italic>
###xml 261 265 261 265 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp8</italic>
###xml 270 274 270 274 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp6</italic>
###xml 302 305 302 305 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">cob</italic>
###xml 310 314 310 314 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad1</italic>
###xml 348 352 348 352 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">rrnS</italic>
###xml 353 357 353 357 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnW</italic>
###xml 362 366 362 366 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnC</italic>
###xml 367 371 367 371 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnM</italic>
###xml 372 376 372 376 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnI</italic>
###xml 464 466 464 466 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR18">18</xref>
###xml 468 470 468 470 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR20">20</xref>
###xml 472 474 472 474 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR23">23</xref>
###xml 476 478 476 478 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR40">40</xref>
###xml 480 482 480 482 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR62">62</xref>
###xml 484 486 484 486 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR63">63</xref>
###xml 562 564 562 564 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR37">37</xref>
###xml 667 669 667 669 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR37">37</xref>
###xml 671 673 671 673 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR39">39</xref>
###xml 675 677 675 677 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR64">64</xref>
###xml 44 60 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
One of the most interesting features in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome is the presence of five major non-coding regions of more than 20 bp: spacer 1 is 22 bp between trnQ and nad2, spacer 2 is 534 bp between trnK and trnD, spacer 3 is 244 bp between atp8 and atp6, spacer 4 is 94 bp between cob and nad1, and spacer 5 is 2325 bp between rrnS-trnW and trnC-trnM-trnI. Long intergenic spacers have been identified in several insect mitochondrial genomes [18, 20, 23, 40, 62, 63]. Although intergenic spacers appeared to be unique to individual species [37], conserved motifs have been found across all insects, and are proposed to be associated with mtTERM [37, 39, 64].
###end p 50

###xml 125 129 125 129 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad2</italic>

###xml 997 1001 997 1001 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">atp6</italic>
###xml 1011 1013 1011 1013 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR65">65</xref>
###xml 1145 1147 1145 1147 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR38">38</xref>
###xml 1149 1151 1149 1151 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR66">66</xref>
###xml 1153 1155 1153 1155 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR67">67</xref>
###xml 1218 1220 1218 1220 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR38">38</xref>
###xml 1222 1224 1222 1224 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR46">46</xref>

###xml 2371 2373 2371 2373 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR68">68</xref>
###xml 2535 2536 2535 2536 <xref xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" ref-type="bibr" rid="CR2">2</xref>

###xml 2860 2866 2860 2866 <label xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Fig.&#160;7</label>
###xml 2910 2915 2910 2915 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">trnS1</italic>
###xml 2920 2924 2920 2924 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">nad1</italic>
###xml 2943 2963 2943 2963 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Evania appendigaster</italic>
###xml 3019 3025 3019 3025 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">Shaded</italic>
###xml 3132 3136 3132 3136 <italic xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink">dots</italic>
###xml 2866 3136 2866 3136 <p xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" textid="53">Alignment of the intergenic spacers between <italic>trnS1</italic> and <italic>nad1</italic> (Spacer 4) across <italic>Evania appendigaster</italic> and other reported hymenopteran mitochondrial genomes. <italic>Shaded</italic> region indicates the conserved motif and some of these unconserved intergenic nucleotides are replaced by <italic>dots</italic></p>
###xml 2866 3136 2866 3136 <caption xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink"><p textid="53">Alignment of the intergenic spacers between <italic>trnS1</italic> and <italic>nad1</italic> (Spacer 4) across <italic>Evania appendigaster</italic> and other reported hymenopteran mitochondrial genomes. <italic>Shaded</italic> region indicates the conserved motif and some of these unconserved intergenic nucleotides are replaced by <italic>dots</italic></p></caption>
###xml 3136 3136 3136 3136 <graphic xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xlink:href="11033_2009_9640_Fig7_HTML" id="MO7"/>
###xml 2860 3136 2860 3136 <fig xmlns:mml="http://www.w3.org/1998/Math/MathML" xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" id="Fig7"><label>Fig.&#160;7</label><caption><p textid="53">Alignment of the intergenic spacers between <italic>trnS1</italic> and <italic>nad1</italic> (Spacer 4) across <italic>Evania appendigaster</italic> and other reported hymenopteran mitochondrial genomes. <italic>Shaded</italic> region indicates the conserved motif and some of these unconserved intergenic nucleotides are replaced by <italic>dots</italic></p></caption><graphic xlink:href="11033_2009_9640_Fig7_HTML" id="MO7"/></fig>
###xml 404 418 <span type="species:ncbi:208481">D. semiclausum</span>
###xml 1285 1301 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 1793 1802 <span type="species:ncbi:32411">P. condei</span>
###xml 1807 1821 <span type="species:ncbi:208481">D. semiclausum</span>
###xml 2660 2676 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">E. appendigaster</span>
###xml 2780 2800 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
###xml 2943 2963 <span type="species:ncbi:27486">Evania appendigaster</span>
Spacer 1 shows limited conservation among hymenopteran species which possess it. In Hymenoptera, the tRNAs directly upstream nad2 are variable because of frequent gene rearrangements of the tRNAs between A+T-rich region and nad2 [23], therefore this spacer is unlikely to have any function in translation or transcription. However, we suggested that it is the product of gene rearrangement as in that in D. semiclausum [23]. Spacer 2 has an A+T content of 96.8%, composed of seven tandem repeat units "GTAATTTTAT", twelve "AATAATAATATT", eight "AATAATAATATTAAT", an initial sequence "TTATTAATAAACCTTAAATTAAAAATTAATTA", and a terminal sequence "AATAATAATAT(TAA)8(TA)33AT". Spacer 3 has an A+T content of 76.2% and contains no repeat sequence although it is 224 bp long. As far as we know, no intergenic nucleotides between atp6 and atp8 have been found in the previously reported insect mitochondrial genomes, and furthermore, it is a common feature of metazoan mitochondrial genomes that atp8 and atp6 overlap [65]. It has been proposed that the secondary structure of the transcribed mRNA may facilitate cleavage between the abutting proteins [38, 66, 67]. We could map secondary structure as those in other insects [38, 46] (Fig. 6), which indicated that the presence of spacer 3 in E. appendigaster would not affect the cleavage of atp6 and atp8. Spacer 4 was found in another six hymenopteran species (Fig. 7). This intergenic spacer region may correspond to the binding site of mtTERM, a transcription attenuation factor [64], as evidenced by a 7 bp motif (ATACTAA) conserved across Lepidoptera [39] and a 5 bp (TACTA) motif conserved across Coleoptera [37]. In Hymenoptera, we found a 6 bp conserved motif (THACWW), which shows high similarity to those in Lepidoptera and Coleoptera. In P. condei and D. semiclausum, although there is only a 2 bp intergenic spacer and a 7 bp overlapping region between trnS1 and nad1, respectively, we could still find conserved motifs in both species nearby regions between trnS1 and nad1. This may indicate wrong annotations of this region in both genomes, or the existence of the motif within genes. Spacer 5 is proposed as the A+T-rich region because of its location between rrnS-trnW and trnC-trnM-trnI and high A+T content (85.6%). It is one of the longest A+T-rich regions in the sequenced insect mitochondrial genomes [23, 68]. Twenty-three tandemly arranged units of "GTCATTATTTAATATAAAATA" are present in the middle of the A+T-rich region. This region, characterized by five elements [2, 5], is believed to function in the initiation of replication and control of transcription. However, these elements in the E. appendigaster mitochondrial genome are not arranged in the conserved pattern.Fig. 6mRNA loops for genes atp8-atp6 in Evania appendigaster mitochondrial genome. The box indicates start codon of atp6Fig. 7Alignment of the intergenic spacers between trnS1 and nad1 (Spacer 4) across Evania appendigaster and other reported hymenopteran mitochondrial genomes. Shaded region indicates the conserved motif and some of these unconserved intergenic nucleotides are replaced by dots
###end p 51
